"No student has ever cleared all three without spending a hit die."

He looks at me.

"You're not a student, Kenji. You never were. Students learn techniques. You learn *principles*. The rock trick — that was an understanding of how a creature perceives the world. The knife in the eye — a predator identifying the one vulnerability that collapses the entire threat. And the sentinel—"

He looks at the destroyed knees.

"You didn't overpower it. You didn't outlast it. You removed its ability to function and took it apart. That's not combat magic. That's *engineering in reverse*."

He pulls a small leather case from his robe. Opens it. A brass token. Wolf-and-keys on one side. An anvil struck by lightning on the other.

"Combat Mage certification. I've given out eleven in forty years. Sera has one. Two members of the King's Guard have one. The rest are dead."

He sets it in my palm.

"You're number twelve. Don't make me regret it."

---

The brass token is warm in my hand. The weight of forty years of standards compressed into a circle of metal smaller than my palm. Eleven people before me. Most of them dead.

I close my fist around it.

The training ground is silent. Morning sun on packed earth and the wreckage of three fights — scored ground, splinters, dark fluid stains, and an Iron Sentinel in three pieces. I'm standing in the middle of it. Thirty-three out of thirty-three hit points. Five hit dice unspent. The ember burning steady and satisfied.

The body disagrees with the ember's satisfaction. Three fights. Multiple Strides. Two ley refills. The metabolism has been burning double since the Speedster perk and right now my stomach is a hollow drum. I need food in the next thirty minutes or the ember starts making withdrawals from hit points.

Somewhere above me — though I don't know it yet — two women stand behind a stone pillar on the second-floor colonnade. One of them has ink-stained fingers pressed against the railing. The other has her hand on the pommel of an arming sword she doesn't remember reaching for.

Neither of them is looking at the destroyed Sentinel.

They're looking at me.

---

END OF CHAPTER NINE — NO LEVEL UP (No Long Rest)

The gauntlet is complete. The morning is young. The Academy still has lessons to teach and secrets to keep. The ember has proved what it can do to the one man in this building qualified to judge it.

Eleven tokens in forty years. Number twelve.

The day isn't over.


# KENJI

## *Day Eight (continued) — What the Ember Sees*

---

I close the token in my fist. The brass is warm.

"Master Aldwin. Thank you."

The grey eyes soften. One degree. Half a second.

"Don't thank me. Thank whatever dropped you in the mud with that fire in your skull." He picks up his staff. "I gave you a test. You gave me a reason to keep teaching."

He pauses at the field's edge.

"Same time tomorrow. Dawn. I'll have something different." The ghost of something that was a smile forty years ago. "Bring the knife trick. I want to see it again."

He shuffles into the colonnade shadow and disappears the way he appeared — like architecture deciding to relocate.

---

The furnace demands fuel. The gauntlet burned through breakfast and then some. I find a food cart near the training grounds — a heavyset woman selling meat pies and roasted apples. Two pies and three apples vanish before she can count her payment.

Zero gold. Zero silver. Zero copper. I am a certified Combat Mage with a brass token and absolutely no money.

The woman's expression shifts toward unpleasant.

"I'll cover it."

Sera. Leaning against the colonnade pillar. Arms folded. The stance says *I happened to be here* and the two copper already between her fingers say *I was waiting*.

She flips them to the cart woman without looking. "He's good for it."

She falls into step beside me.

"Your schedule," she says. Professional voice. But her eyes keep drifting to the brass token. "Midday — Elara's theory lesson. Private session. Room twelve. She said to bring the ember and an open mind. Also to eat first."

Second finger. "Afternoon — free. Library's open. Training grounds available. Garrett sold the surplus weapons for eighteen gold. Wants to discuss guild business at dinner."

Third finger. "Tomorrow dawn — Aldwin again. Then the vault tour in the afternoon. And Edwyn's presentation to the theological faculty. He'd like us there."

She's leading me somewhere through the colonnade. Toward the east wing.

"Kenji."

"Yeah."

"That thing with the Stalker. The knife. When did you learn Radiant Edge could infuse a thrown weapon that returns to your hand?"

"About three seconds before I threw it."

Silence. Four steps. Five.

"You improvised a new combat technique in the middle of a fight with a paralytic ambush predator in supernatural darkness."

"It worked."

"That's not the point." She stops. Turns. "The point is that you keep doing things that shouldn't be possible and treating them like they're obvious."

She looks at the token in my hand.

"Aldwin gave you the certification. He's given eleven. I'm one of them. It took me three years and a field examination that nearly killed me." A pause. "You got yours on your first morning."

Something on her face. Not jealousy. The vertigo of watching someone climb a mountain by a route that isn't on any map.

"You earned it," she says quietly. "I watched."

A beat.

"Don't tell Elara I was there. She told me not to come."

"But she was there too."

Sera's expression flickers. Her thumb runs along the sword pommel — the unconscious tell, the one she doesn't know she has. "She told both of us not to come. We came anyway. Separately. Ended up behind the same pillar." A pause. "It was awkward."

---

Room twelve. The paper avalanche has grown. New stacks on the windowsill. A cleared space on the desk already being reclaimed. A chalkboard propped against the bookshelf — diagrams, circles, connecting lines, symbols I don't recognise.

Elara is at the chalkboard. Chalk dust joining the ink stains. She doesn't turn.

"Close the door."

The latch clicks. The corridor sounds go muffled. The predator's eyes catch the reason — silver lines running along the doorframe, window edges, floor perimeter. Wards. Not containment. Surveillance countermeasures. She's soundproofed her own study against eavesdropping.

She turns. The dark eyes do the sweep-that-stalls. But today the theoretical curiosity is gone. She's seen the gauntlet. Something sharper has replaced it.

"Sit."

I find the chair. The only clear surface in the room.

She pulls a second chair close. Four feet between us. The chalkboard behind her. Ledger on her knee. Fresh page.

"I'm going to be direct. Yesterday I asked what you are. You made a joke and winked at my contractor." The ink-stained fingers tap the ledger. "Today I need real answers. Not because I'm curious — because what I saw this morning changes things."

She pauses.

"I told Sera and myself not to go. We both went. I saw everything."

No pretense.

"Three academy-grade specimens. You cleared all three without a meaningful hit. You improvised a radiant-infused returning knife throw through supernatural darkness into an eye socket. You dismantled a construct's engineering with precision our fourth-years can't match."

She leans forward.

"But that's not what frightened me. The ember. I could see it with mage-sight. The energy signature was visible from the colonnade. And what I saw was not sorcery. Not wizardry. Not divine casting. Not any classification in three hundred years of Academy taxonomy."

She picks up the chalk. Draws a circle.

"This is how magic works. For everyone."

Lines radiating outward. The triangle — source, will, effect.

"Wizards have weak sources but powerful will — precision through study. Sorcerers have powerful sources but less control — instinct. Priests have external sources — divine energy through faith."

She taps the triangle.

"Every practitioner in history fits inside this triangle."

She turns.

"You don't fit."

A second circle. Larger. Lines radiating *inward*. Converging on a center point.

"Your source isn't generating energy. It *is* energy. The ember isn't a talent or a connection. It's a *force*. Raw creation. When you cast, you're not shaping energy into an effect. You're allowing the energy to express itself through your will. The relationship is collaborative, not hierarchical."

She sets the chalk down.

"That's why you develop new techniques mid-combat. The ember responds to necessity in real time because it's not following a formula. It's *creating* one. Every spell you cast is being invented at the moment of casting."

She sits. Opens the ledger.

"I need you to reach for the ember. Not to cast. Not to infuse. Just feel what it is. And describe it to me."

---

I close my eyes.

The room disappears. The paper. The chalkboard. Elara. All replaced by the interior landscape I've visited in fragments since the mud.

The ember.

It's always there. But reaching for it without purpose is different. Like looking at the sun after only ever using it to see by.

"It's warm. Always warm. But not temperature. The warmth of something that's *there*. Completely. Without doubt."

Chalk scratches on the ledger.

"It has depth. Not size — *depth*. When I first woke up it felt like a candle. Now it feels like a well. Every time I push it, the bottom drops further. I haven't found the floor."

"Describe the texture."

"It's not separate from me. When I reach for it I'm reaching for myself. A part that was always there but wasn't turned on." A pause. "No. It was always on. I didn't know how to listen."

The ember pulses. Agreeing.

"It has opinions. It doesn't talk. It has preferences. Weapons — yes, always. Protection — yes. The Blade Ward came naturally. Like the ember already knew how."

"Things it refuses?"

"Utility. I asked for night vision. Flat no. Cold. Disinterested. Like asking a sword to stir soup. But then I framed it as Eyes of the Hunter — predator vision, target acquisition — and it couldn't infuse fast enough. The intent matters. The framing matters. If I approach it as a weapon, it responds. As a tool, silence."

Elara's breathing quickens.

"And creation. The altar."

The memory. Gold and black. The cycle.

"That was different. That wasn't the ember being a weapon. It was the ember being *itself*. The truest expression. Not force, not light. *Creation*. The fundamental act of making something exist. I poured it into the god and it didn't fight the entropy. It *completed* it. Two halves of a sentence finding each other."

Silence. The chalk has stopped.

"Open your eyes."

I do.

She's pale. White. The ledger covered in frantic shorthand. The chalk broken in her fingers. One hand has risen without her noticing — hovering in the air between us, ink-stained fingertips reaching toward something only she can see. Her dark eyes fixed on a point two inches in front of my chest.

"Don't move. The ember is still open. I can see it with mage-sight. The energy signature is—"

She swallows. The hovering hand trembles. A scholar's hand. Fourteen years of careful, measured, documented work — and it's shaking.

"It's the most beautiful thing I've ever seen."

The words escape before the scientist catches them. She blinks. Resets. But the crack is there.

"The signature is generative. Not emitting energy — emitting *potential*. The difference between a fire and a seed. Your ember is an infinite seed that keeps becoming without ever finishing."

She stands. Paces.

"Creation and entropy aren't opposites — they're phases. The same energy in different directions. And you're carrying one half of that engine inside your chest."

She sits back down. Slower.

"Kenji. I need to tell you something."

The ink-stained fingers grip the ledger.

"For three years I've been tracking a pattern. Graduates who received their Assignment Seals have been declining. Slowly. Their magical abilities diminish over months and years. They become less sharp. Less powerful. Most chalk it up to stress."

She looks at the warded door.

"It's not stress. Something is draining them. The seal has been corrupted. Modified. It's acting as a siphon — drawing magical essence and funneling it somewhere."

She pushes her sleeve back. Her left inner forearm — a mark. Stylized seal. Academy insignia. The size of a coin.

"I received mine eight years ago. I'm being drained too. I thought it was age. It's not."

The fear underneath everything since yesterday. Named at last.

"I don't know who corrupted the seals. I don't know where the energy goes. I don't know how deep it reaches." She grips the ledger. "But whatever is receiving it — whatever is feeding on twelve years of graduates — is hungry. And it's getting closer to full."

Eight days. I've been in this world eight days. I came looking for training and found a conspiracy that could kill hundreds. The INT of nine wants to simplify. The CHA of seventeen is already mapping who to talk to, who to leverage, who to trust. And the ember — the ember just found something that offends it on a level deeper than thought.

The nighthollow. Voss. The highway operation.

"I think it's connected. Someone inside this Academy is funneling resources outward — sedatives, money, influence — to maintain a network that protects whatever is happening underground." She looks at the floor. "Sub-basement level two manufactures the nighthollow. Level three is restricted. No student has ever accessed it."

She looks at me.

"You walked into a cellar and touched a dying god. You carry creation energy — the one force that could theoretically detect corrupted entropy in the seals."

She holds out her left wrist. The seal facing me.

"I'm asking you to touch my seal. Reach for the ember. Not to cast — to feel. If the seal is corrupted with entropy, the creation energy should react."

Her eyes are steady. Her hand is shaking.

I look her deep in the eyes. Pause for a moment. Awkwardly.

"You want me to touch your *what*?"

---

The silence stretches.

The fear in her eyes transforms. Confusion. Processing. The exact moment the double meaning lands.

Color rises from her collar. The ink-stained fingers retract. The wrist vanishes into the sleeve.

"My *seal*, Kenji. The Academy seal. On my *wrist*." Each word enunciated with the precision of a woman who has taught for fourteen years and never once had a student say *that* in a warded room. "The magical mark that I just spent five minutes explaining is potentially draining my life force."

She stands. Sits. Stands again.

"I am trying to show you evidence of a conspiracy that may be killing hundreds of graduates and you're — you —"

She stops. Turns.

"Sera warned me. She said *he does this*. I thought she was exaggerating."

A beat.

"She was not exaggerating."

She sits down. Aggressively. Pushes a strand of hair behind her ear with controlled fury.

"Are you going to help me or are you going to make jokes while a potentially existential threat gathers power beneath the building we're sitting in?"

The wrist again. The seal. The hand no longer shaking.

Rigid.

"*Touch. The seal.*"

I grin. "Yes ma'am."

---

I take her wrist. Gently. The seal under my thumb — raised, warm, magic-warm. I reach for the ember. The open reach. The listening reach.

The ember touches the seal.

The world drops away.

The surface first — legitimate enchantment. Classification matrix. Elara's specialty. Her assignment. Her graduation year. Normal. Clean.

Beneath that.

The ember recoils. Not in pain. In *recognition*.

Entropy.

I know this feeling. The cellar. The altar. The same flavor — cold, pull, patient hunger. But not the same god.

The Duskfen entity was vast and desperate and lonely. What I feel in Elara's seal is different. Smaller. Precise. Not gasping — *sipping*. A thin thread of entropy embedded in the seal's enchantment like a parasite in healthy tissue. Drawing from Elara — not much, not fast. A trickle so subtle the body adjusts the way it adjusts to a slow bleed.

The thread leads down. Through the seal, through the ley web, through stone and ward and darkness. Into the bones of the Academy. It doesn't end at a god gasping through a crack. It ends at something *deliberate*. Something placed with precision and patience and the confidence of a craftsman who knows his work won't be examined.

And at the far end — distant, muffled by layers of stone and ancient warding — a pulse. Faint. Rhythmic. Like a heartbeat. Something receiving the trickle. Collecting. Growing fuller.

The ember flares. Hot. Angry. Not at the entropy — at the *design*. The Duskfen god was starving and took what it could reach. This is architecture. Someone *built* this. Someone wove entropy into a seal of achievement and turned every graduate into an unwitting battery.

The creation energy pushes against the thread. Instinctive. Protective. The thread *flinches*. For one instant the trickle stops.

Elara gasps. Her fingers clench around mine.

Then the thread reasserts. The parasitic draw resumes. The ember could burn it out — I feel the capacity — but the thread is woven into the seal itself. Burning it means burning the seal. And I don't know what that would do to her.

I let go.

---

The room. The paper. The chalkboard. Elara's face — white. Eyes wide. Fingers still gripping mine.

"You felt that," she whispers. "The drain stopped. For one second. The first time in eight years that I've felt..." She searches. "...*whole*."

My hand is trembling. Not weakness. Anger. The ember is furious — burning hot with the particular rage of creation encountering something that corrupts creation itself. Turning achievement into theft.

"It's there. Exactly what you suspected. Entropy woven into the seal underneath the legitimate enchantment. Siphoning your essence in a constant trickle. So slow you'd never notice."

"Where does it go?"

"Down. Through the ley web. Into the deep structure of the Academy. Something at the other end is receiving. Collecting. It has a pulse — like a heartbeat."

"How many years."

"You said twelve years. If every seal is corrupted—"

"Three hundred and forty-seven graduates." The number sits in the room like a weight. "Three hundred and forty-seven slow-burn siphons feeding something beneath this building for over a decade."

"Can you remove it? The thread. You stopped it for a moment."

"I could. The ember has the force. But the thread is woven into the seal. Removing it might damage you. I'd need the original seal design — the uncorrupted version. Compare the clean design to what's actually there, map where the entropy was inserted, find how to remove it safely."

She nods. The scholar understanding.

"The original designs are in the Academy archives. Restricted section. Accessible only to senior faculty and—"

She stops.

"—the Chancellor."

The name.

"Chancellor Marius Vael controls the archives. He controls enrollment. He controls the sealing ceremony. He's controlled all of it for the last twelve years."

The calculation she didn't want to make.

"I don't have proof. Correlation isn't causation. But—"

"But you don't believe in coincidences."

"No. I don't."

She looks at the chalkboard. The circles. The triangle.

"We need the original seal design. We need the restricted archives. And we need to get into sub-basement level three." She looks at me. "None of that is possible without the Chancellor's authorization or breaking into the most heavily warded sections of the Academy."

A pause.

"You said Ryn taught you to pick locks."

---

END OF CHAPTER TEN — NO LEVEL UP (No Long Rest)

The conspiracy is open. The threads are visible. Three hundred and forty-seven graduates draining into something that pulses like a heartbeat beneath the Academy. A Chancellor who controls everything. A warded archive with the answers. And a sub-basement that no student has ever accessed.

The ember is angry. Creation has found something that corrupts creation itself.

The afternoon is young. The questions are old. And somewhere beneath my feet, something is getting fuller.


# KENJI

## *Day Eight (continued) — What's Underneath*

---

I find Garrett in the market district. Outdoor table near a weapons stall. A tankard and a ledger he didn't have yesterday. The liaison building infrastructure.

"How was the old man?"

"I killed three monsters, got a brass token, and made two women regret spying on me."

"So a normal morning." He pushes a chair out. "Sit. I've got numbers."

The surplus weapons sold — longbows, crossbows, short swords, bolts and arrows. Eighteen gold total. Already deposited in a holding account at a moneylender on Merchant Row. The guild needs a treasury that isn't a lockbox.

My income — ten percent of guild earnings. The guild hasn't earned anything yet beyond the weapon sale. The highway contract won't be formalized for three or four days. Once active, forty gold per month flows in. My cut — four gold monthly.

"Short version — you're broke right now. The guild has eighteen gold in holding but that's operating capital. Brindle needs weapons, rations, and at least two more recruits before the contract activates. A garrison that can't feed itself doesn't last a month."

He looks at my belt.

"What have you got to sell?"

I lay it out. Voss's keys — unknown locks, hold them. Flint stones — ammunition, keep them. Pip's honey cakes — he looks at me, looks at the cakes, doesn't ask. The entropy anchor ring — might be worth something at the Gilt Lens. The Combat Mage token — not for sale. Ever.

"Honest assessment — you've got nothing to sell except maybe the ring."

He pushes five gold across the table.

"Advance on your founder's share. Meals, flint, incidentals for the week." He looks at me. "Don't spend it on enchanted knives."

---

The Silver Draft. Edwyn's table. The same table, the same ledger, the same tea. He's turned a corner of the common room into a field office. Notes spread in organized stacks — the presentation taking shape.

"You're not injured. That's new for this time of day."

"Give it time." I set the returning knife on the table. "I need more poison for this. Sleep or paralysis. Something non-lethal."

He examines the blade. Studies the surface.

"Somnus — what Maren sold you — I can't replicate. The refinement requires equipment I don't have." He holds up a finger. "But."

Three items from his satchel. A cloth pouch. A glass jar. A dark bundle of leaves.

Three options. Slumber paste — brightcap mushrooms concentrated into a topical sedative. Disadvantage on everything for a minute, second hit knocks unconscious. Four doses, two hours prep. Lockjoint resin — staghorn cap spores disrupting muscle control. Half speed, no reaction, one action only, three rounds. Three doses, four hours prep.

And bittershade.

"Rendered differently — cold extraction instead of heated — it produces a nerve toxin. Convulsions. Full incapacitation. Five minutes. They're conscious but can't move, can't speak. They feel everything."

He sets the leaves down.

"This one is a *poison*, not a sedative. The distinction matters to me even if it doesn't matter to the blade."

"I'll take the bittershade. I'll pick it up at your presentation."

He nods. The professional accepting. The priest filing the weight.

"When you use it — remember the target is conscious. They feel everything."

"Noted."

I set the brass token on the table. His eyebrows climb slowly.

"Combat Mage certification. On your first day." He sets it down gently. The priest's fingers handle it the way they handle relics — with the weight of what it represents rather than what it's made of. "There are faculty who've taught here twenty years and never earned one."

"Aldwin said I'm number twelve."

"In *forty years*." He shakes his head. "You know, when I met you in that clearing, I thought the Sovereign had sent me a project. Turns out He sent me a front-row seat." "Tomorrow. Second bell, afternoon. Main lecture hall, west wing. I'd like you there — not as support. As evidence. Having the man who touched the altar in the room reduces skepticism."

"I'll be there."

"And eat before you come."

---

I pull a honey cake from my chest pocket. Pip's handwriting on the cloth. *Come back. — P*

Three days old. Not preserved — the cakes were in my pocket, not the satchel. Slightly stale. The lavender faded. A hairline crack down the middle where the road put its weight on it.

I eat it anyway. It tastes like a girl standing in a doorway. Like someone who believes you'll keep a promise you haven't figured out how to make yet.

Two cakes remaining. I transfer them into the Satchel of Holding. Preserved now.

---

The Gilt Lens. The bell chimes. Maren Holt behind the counter. Same spectacles. Same magnifying glass.

"Back already. Spent all your gold and you want more things."

"Appraisal today."

"One gold standard. Two if it's cursed."

I set the entropy anchor ring on the counter. Still wrapped in cloth.

"Don't touch it directly."

Her eyebrow rises. Heavy leather gloves — rune-stitched, for dangerous objects. She unwraps the cloth. The ring on the counter. Small. Iron. A dull black stone that catches the ward-light and holds it. Light enters and doesn't come back.

Magnifying glass first. Then a crystal lens — pale blue, faceted. The predator's eyes catch what happens: the lens reveals micro-enchantments inside the stone. Dozens of threadlike structures converging on the center.

"Where did you get this."

Not a question. A demand wearing a question's clothes. The magnifying glass is steady but the spectacles have slid down her nose and she hasn't pushed them back. Maren Holt always pushes them back.

"A cellar beneath a farmhouse in Duskfen."

She's quiet for a long time.

"This isn't ancient. The iron is old — a century, maybe two. But the enchantment is older. Significantly. The stone predates the setting by a margin I'm not comfortable estimating."

She looks at me.

"This is an entropy siphon. The stone absorbs ambient magical energy and channels it along a predetermined path. The micro-enchantments are routing threads directing absorbed energy to a specific destination."

She taps the counter beside the ring.

"The structure is sophisticated. This isn't hedge magic. This is institutional-grade enchantment work."

*Institutional-grade*. In a city with one institution.

"To a collector — fifteen to twenty gold. To a researcher — fifty or more." She looks at me. "To you — it's evidence. And evidence is worth more than gold."

One gold for the appraisal. Four gold remaining.

---

Room twelve. I knock. One dark eye in the gap.

"I told you to—" She sees my face. The door opens.

I set the ring on her desk. Tell her everything Maren said. The iron. The stone. The routing threads. Institutional-grade.

Elara sits. Pulls her own crystal lens. Holds it over the ring.

Two minutes of silence. Her free hand writing without looking.

"The routing threads. The encoding pattern. I've seen this before."

A worn leather folder. Pages of hand-drawn diagrams. Three years of work.

"I've been trying to reverse-engineer the entropy threads in the seals. Too sophisticated. Too old. Didn't match any modern methodology."

She sets one of her diagrams next to the ring. Crystal lens over both.

"Because it's not modern."

She looks up.

"The encoding pattern in this ring is the same pattern as the entropy threads in the seals. Same methodology. Same architect."

She stops.

"Or the architect is still alive," I say.

The wards hum. The ley web pulses.

"The Chancellor is old. Visibly old. He's been Chancellor for twelve years. Before that, senior faculty for fifteen. Already old when he arrived."

She looks at the ring and the diagram.

"What if he was already old because he was *already old*. This methodology is centuries old. If the same person designed this ring and corrupted the seals..."

She looks at me.

"Then Marius Vael is not an elderly Chancellor. He's something much older wearing the face of one."

"Keep the ring," I tell her.

She wraps it back in cloth. Holds it out. "You keep it. When you're in his office — the ember might tell you more."

I take the ring back. Evidence that connects a farmhouse cellar to an Academy sub-basement. Same threads. Same architect. Centuries apart.

---

I find Sera at the stone owl fountain. Cleaning her sword. Afternoon light on the blade.

I drop two copper into her lap.

She looks at the coins. "I was going to let that debt build. See how long before your pride caught up." She pockets them. "Six hours. Not bad."

I sit on the fountain edge beside her. Students thinning in the courtyard. Afternoon classes ending.

"I need to talk to you about something."

The sword goes back in the scabbard.

"How hard would it be to sneak into sub-basement level three. Tonight."

"Sub-basement three. The restricted level that no student has ever accessed. In an Academy with enchanted guards and ward systems refined for three hundred years." She looks at me. "Why."

I don't answer why. Not yet. Instead I ask a different question.

"Are we close enough for me to touch your seal?"

One second. Two. Her hand on the sword pommel goes still.

The CHA of seventeen knows exactly what it's doing. The INT of nine is just happy to be here.

"Your seal. The Combat Mage certification. Aldwin gave you one."

"My *what*."

"I saw the mark on your forearm during training at Duskfen. Same system. Same Academy."

Her eyes narrow. The color hasn't arrived yet — she's holding it back through sheer force of will.

"Elara warned me. She sent a note. Three words. *He does this.*"

A beat.

"You asked Elara the same question."

"Technically she offered."

"She *offered* to let you—"

She stops. Closes her eyes. The color arrives with reinforcements.

"Kenji. I just met you eight days ago. You've fought a god, founded a guild, made a killer swear loyalty, and earned a token that took me three years of nearly dying. And twice now you've asked a woman to let you touch her seal with a face that belongs in a brothel."

She stares at me. Color in her ears.

"What exactly are you checking for."

---

I don't answer that question either. Instead I say something I've been thinking since the training grounds.

"Sera. It just occurs to me — you have a rare token signifying you're an elite battle mage. Yet I've never seen you cast a spell."

The words land like a stone in still water.

Her expression doesn't change. That's how I know it hit.

Five seconds.

"I'm a fighter. The certification recognizes integrated combat — magic and steel."

"But you fight with steel. Only steel. Every fight I've seen. Not once have you cast."

"Combat magic requires focus. Field conditions aren't—"

"Sera."

She stops.

"When's the last time you cast a spell."

The silence changes. Not defensive. The silence of someone hearing the ground crack beneath something they've been avoiding.

"Two years." Quiet. The quietest I've ever heard her voice. Her hand drops from the sword pommel to her lap — the first time I've seen her voluntarily release the weapon. "I haven't been able to cast in two years. I told myself it was field rust. That if I trained, it would come back."

She closes her fists. Opens them. The fingers that should crackle with force magic flex against nothing.

"It hasn't come back. I've been here two days and I've tried. In my room. Alone. Force bolts, shield projections, blade enchantments — gone. Not weak. Gone. Like reaching for a shelf that used to have books on it and finding empty wood."

She looks at me. The mask cracked. Not the hairline fracture from the bridge. A real crack.

"I took the Duskfen contract because I thought if I got back into real danger, the magic would have to come back. Survival instinct." Her voice steady. The steadiness of a rehearsed confession never spoken aloud. "It didn't. Every fight since Duskfen — the Hexcrawlers, the bandits, the bridge — I fought like a soldier. Because it's all I have left."

She looks at the brass token in my hand.

"I earned that certification with magic I can't do anymore."

She looks at me.

"You know why. Don't you."

---

"Yes, Sera. I understand you're guarded." I stare into her eyes. "Maybe all you need for the magic to come back is for something magical to happen. I know we don't have the privacy of your room and all, but I'll be quick. With your permission, I just need to rub your seal for a moment."

The journey her face takes starts at raw vulnerability, passes through disbelief, accelerates through fury, and arrives at a destination without a name. The color doesn't rise. It *detonates*.

"You — I — that's not —"

A student glances over. Sera's death-glare. The student walks faster.

"I am going to kill you. Not today. Today I need you alive. But it's on the calendar."

She stares at her palm. Then extends her left forearm. Pushes the bracer back. The Combat Mage seal — smaller than Elara's, different insignia, same Academy mark.

"Do it. And if you make one more comment about rubbing anything, I will break your hand."

---

I take her forearm. Fingers find the seal. Magic-warm. Wrong-warm.

The ember touches it.

The same surface. Certification matrix. Aldwin's signature in arcane shorthand. Clean on top.

Underneath — the thread. The same entropy parasite. The same encoding. But *worse*. The certification seal has more surface area than a graduation seal. More integration points. The parasite has a wider pipe. And it's been draining for three years.

The shelf with empty books. The magic that won't come back. The thread didn't diminish it. It *emptied* it. The slow bleed became a hemorrhage because the wider seal gave the parasite more to hold onto.

Sera's magical essence isn't atrophied. It's been *stolen*.

The ember flares. Hotter than Elara's reading. Because this isn't an academic researcher. It's the woman who taught me the cage. Who planned the boulder ambush. Who carried me out of a cellar. Who watched from a colonnade she wasn't supposed to be on and said *you earned it*.

The creation energy pushes against the thread. Hard. The thread flinches. The drain stutters. Stops.

Sera gasps.

Her free hand grabs my wrist. Eyes wide. Not pain — the opposite. The absence of something she'd carried so long she forgot it was there.

"Kenji — what — *what is that* —"

Her right hand comes up. Palm open. A flicker. Faint. Blue-white. The ghost of a force bolt that hasn't existed in two years. It sparks once. Twice. Gutters. Dies.

But it was *there*.

The thread reasserts. The drain resumes. The flicker goes dark.

Sera stares at her empty palm.

"It was there," she whispers. "For a second. It was there."

She looks at me. The mask gone. Completely. Someone younger underneath. Someone who went to an Academy and learned to throw force bolts and believed in what she was becoming.

"What's happening to me, Kenji?"

---

"Nothing. I just have that effect on women. Now that I got you off, I need a plan to get into sub-basement three this evening. Your plans are way better than mine, so... get to planning."

The words land like a grenade in a library.

"You — did you just — *got me off*?!"

A student turns. Sera's death-glare. The student accelerates.

"The calendar is getting crowded, Kenji." Her voice is flat. The flatness of a woman updating a list she started ten minutes ago.

She stares at her empty palm. The two seconds she was whole. Given and taken away by the man grinning at her on a fountain.

The fist closes. The jaw sets. The machine clicks into place.

"Sub-basement three. Tonight. You're insane." She looks at the Academy. "But you're not wrong."

She's already working. Eyes moving across architecture.

"Give me what you know."

I give her what I have. Sub-basement two manufactures nighthollow. Level three below that — restricted, never accessed. Elara's tried and failed.

"I've been mapping internal security for two days. Guards work shifts — four main gate, two ground floor, two sub-basement entrance on the west side. Shift change at midnight. Six-minute window — outgoing pair walks up, incoming walks down. Nobody watching anything."

She draws on the wet stone.

"That's your window into level one. Research resident with a Combat Mage token and a confident walk bluffs past questions."

Second line. "Level two. Ward locks. Keyed to faculty. You can't pick those." She looks at me. "But Elara can."

Third line. "Level three. Unknown. No guard rotation — either they don't know it exists or access is controlled by something other than guards."

Two approaches. The bluff through the front using the shift change. Or the crawl — ventilation shafts, drainage channels, ley conduit maintenance passages. Three hundred years of infrastructure running through the building's bones.

"Both need Elara for level two. Both need me because you're a combat mage, not a thief."

One condition.

"When we find what's down there — whatever is feeding on three hundred and forty-seven people including *me* — you tell me everything. Whatever Elara told you in that warded room. Whatever the ember showed you. Everything."

Dark eyes. Steady. The crack visible.

"I've earned that. On a bridge and in a cellar and on a colonnade I wasn't supposed to be on."

---

"Alright. Option two — the crawl. We all meet down there. Honestly I was barely paying attention to Elara. She asked me to touch her seal and she started moaning and gasping... just like you a few seconds ago. I'll have Elara give you a recap during the crawl."

I hop off the fountain. Walk away before Sera can kill me.

"She was NOT — I did NOT — that is not what *gasping* —"

I'm already walking. The Windrunner Boots carrying me at a pace that's technically not running.

"KENJI."

I don't turn around. The predator's eyes catch her reflection in a window — fists clenched, color visible from thirty feet, mouth forming words the courtyard should never absorb.

A student near the fountain looks at Sera. Looks at me. Quietly closes his textbook and relocates.

I make it around the corner before the laugh comes. Real. Full. The first from pure joy since the mud.

The ember pulses. Warm. Amused. Even creation has a sense of humor.

---

Evening. The Silver Draft. Shepherd's pie. A second shepherd's pie. The boy has stopped making eye contact.

Garrett's out — a note says *Following a lead on guild contracts. Back by morning. Don't do anything stupid without me.* He knows me well enough already.

Edwyn's in his room. The chemical tang of bittershade through his door.

The evening darkens. Eyes of the Hunter fades. The world goes normal. Arcane Stride fades. Normal speed. Normal weight. Just a man in a room.

Not for long.

---

11:45 PM.

Gear up. Light configuration — no chest piece, no shoulder guards. Underlayer and bracers only. Windrunner Boots. Satchel of Holding cross-body. Returning Somnus Knife on belt. Lockpick set. Flint stones. Hand axe — compact, concealable. Longsword left behind — too conspicuous underground.

Two spells in the dark.

Eyes of the Hunter. The world sharpens. Twelve hours.

Arcane Stride. Silver hum in the legs. Twelve hours.

Back door. Alley. The Academy district at midnight — empty streets, closed shops, the pale tower catching moonlight. The ley web pulsing beneath the cobblestones.

---

The Academy's west side. A service door half-hidden behind an ivy-covered buttress.

Two shapes in the shadows.

Sera. Dark leathers. Sword on hip. Hair pulled back. The face of a woman on a mission.

Elara. Almost unrecognizable. Dark trousers, fitted jacket, soft-soled boots. Hair hidden under dark cloth. She looks like a woman who planned to never do this and prepared for it anyway.

"You're late," Sera says.

"I'm two minutes early."

"I've been here twenty." She looks at Elara. "She's been here thirty."

Elara's ink-stained fingers grip a small satchel. Tools clinking.

"The maintenance channel access is through sub-basement two. I open the ward lock. The ley conduit hatch is in the northeast corner — behind the distillation array. The conduit runs vertically through the building's core. It connects every level including—"

She looks down.

"—whatever is below."

Sera looks at me. Then at Elara.

"Did you brief her?"

"I told her to ask you for the details on the way down."

"You told me to ask Elara for a recap."

"I told you Elara was gasping."

Elara's head turns. Slowly. The dark eyes find me.

"He said *what*."

"We should get moving."

---

END OF CHAPTER ELEVEN — NO LEVEL UP (No Long Rest)

Three people at a door at midnight. Two of them want to kill me. All three of us are about to descend into something that's been feeding on this Academy for twelve years.

The ember burns steady. The creation energy that completed a dying god, tamed a creature of entropy, and gave a woman back two seconds of stolen magic.

Whatever's underneath — it's built from the opposite of what I carry. And unlike the god in the cellar, it didn't get there by accident.

Someone put it there. And someone has been feeding it.

Time to find out who.

# KENJI

## *Day Eight (concluded) — The Crawl*

---

Elara opens the service door. Faculty key. Oiled hinges. The maintenance corridor descends into dark.

"Before we go down," Sera says. Quiet. Hard. "The briefing. Now."

I nod at Elara. She talks fast. Three minutes. The seal corruption. The entropy threads. Three hundred and forty-seven graduates. The siphon leading down. The pulse — heartbeat, collecting, growing fuller. The encoding match between the Duskfen ring and the seals. Same architect. Centuries old. The Chancellor.

"And my seal," Sera says when Elara finishes.

"The certification seal has a wider channel. The drain has been—"

"More complete." Flat. "Three years. Not atrophied. Stolen."

"Yes."

Sera looks at the dark corridor.

"Let's go find it."

---

Sub-basement one. General storage. I take point — the predator's eyes turning darkness transparent. Sera behind me. Elara last, navigating by memory and touch.

"You've done this before," Sera whispers. Not a question.

"Twice. Both times ended badly for someone who wasn't me." Elara's voice is steady. The scholar has a spine made of iron and secrets.

The midnight shift change — voices, boots, the roster exchange forty feet away through stone. We hold. Three people breathing in the dark. Sera's hand on my shoulder — a pressure that says *stop* and *I'm here* in the same touch. Six minutes. The voices fade.

Sera's hand signals. *Move. Left. Twenty feet. Door.*

The ward lock on sub-basement two. Elara's palm. The shimmer reads her signature and dissolves.

---

Sub-basement two. The alchemical laboratories. Chemical tang. Workbenches. Glassware. Distillation apparatus.

The predator's eyes find it immediately — a distillation array on the northeast wall, condensation in the collection flask. Dark. Nearly black.

Nighthollow.

The production setup. Botanical compounds. Mineral reagents. Institutional equipment — requisitioned, logged, maintained. Not a rogue operation. A sanctioned laboratory used for unsanctioned purpose.

"Faculty-grade extraction setup," Elara says. "Someone signed for this through official channels."

The northeast corner. Behind the distillation array. The maintenance hatch — iron, recessed in the floor, wheel-lock mechanism. No ward shimmer. Purely mechanical. The ley conduit access.

I turn the wheel-lock. Stiff. Unused. A quarter turn. Half. Full. The lock disengages with a *clunk* that sounds like a gunshot.

Silence. No alarm. No footsteps.

The hatch opens. A vertical shaft. Three feet wide. Iron rungs. Descending into darkness.

The air that rises is cold. Not cellar-cold. The cold of entropy. Concentrated. Thick. The same flavor as the Brennick cellar. As Elara's seal. As Sera's seal. But denser.

The ember contracts. Shields itself. A flame when wind hits — not extinguished. Defended.

---

Thirty feet down. The predator's eyes straining. Another hatch. Sub-basement three.

This hatch is different. Black threads — hairline-thin — woven into the iron frame. Entropy-based sensor. Not blocking. Detecting. Anything with magical energy that crosses the threshold gets flagged.

"Your boots are enchanted," Elara says. "The knife has a return enchantment. The satchel is dimensional. If you go through, the sensor triggers."

But I have something else. The Entropy Bond. I touched a Hexcrawler. I touched a dying god. The ember has a relationship with entropy. Not opposition. Dialogue.

I reach toward the black threads. Hovering. The open hand. The listening reach. Creation meeting entropy to understand.

The ember touches the threads. They're not alive. But they have a shape. A logic. Instructions — *detect, report*. I push gently. Not burning. Quieting. Like laying a hand over a sleeping animal.

The threads dim. Dormant.

"It's down. Go. Now."

Sera through. Elara through. Me last — the ember holding the suppression as I pass. The threads twitch. I release. The ward hums back to life.

We're through.

---

Sub-basement three.

The predator's eyes struggle for the first time. Not dark — *too dark*. Entropy concentration so dense it interferes with the Eyes. Sixty feet of darkvision drops to thirty. Shadows at the edges that shouldn't be there.

The air is cold. The cold of absence. My breath doesn't fog — the moisture consumed before it can condense.

A corridor. Stone. Older than the Academy — rough-hewn, undressed. This was here first. The institution built on top of whatever this is. The ley conduit channels glow faintly — pale blue threads converging ahead. Flowing toward the heart.

And the pulse. Physical now. A vibration in the stone. Thump. Thump. Thump.

Sera whispers. "I can feel it. The pull. The same thing I felt when you touched my seal — except everywhere."

Elara. Hand flat on the wall. "The ley conduits are converging. Every thread from every seal. This is the terminus."

We advance. Elara's boot catches a loose stone. The sound rings.

The pulse *changes*. Shifts rhythm. Something noticed.

"It knows we're here."

Sera's sword comes up. "Then we stop sneaking."

---

The chamber.

Circular. Fifty feet across. Vaulted ceiling lost in entropy haze. Rough-hewn walls covered in carvings — old, worn, the root language of the encoding from the seals and the ring. Every ley conduit thread converges here.

At the center. A stone pedestal. Three feet high.

A crown.

Blackened iron circlet. Runes carved into every surface — the same encoding from the ring and the seals but orders of magnitude more complex. The runes *move*. Crawling across the iron. The ley threads flow into the crown from every direction. Dozens of them.

Thump. Thump. Thump.

The heartbeat. The source. The thing collecting the essence of three hundred and forty-seven graduates for twelve years.

The ember *screams*. Not sound. Sensation. Hot. Bright. Furious. Creation encounters entropy enslaved — chained to a purpose it was never meant to serve. A cosmic force perverted into a feeding machine.

And behind the pedestal. In the deepest shadow. A shape. Not moving. *Present*. Tall. Thin. Patient. Something waiting for a very long time.

The predator's eyes resolve it at the limit of their range. Not a construct. Not a creature. A *presence*. Darkness given form — but not the Duskfen god's desperate, gasping darkness. This is entropy with architecture. Emaciated limbs like winter branches. A silhouette that frays at the edges, wisps of green-black energy curling off the shape like smoke from a candle that burns cold. Two points of cold light where eyes should be — not the rage of something hungry. The patience of something that has been counting its meals for twelve years.

The cold light finds me across thirty feet.

Not my body. My ember.

***...you carry the seed...***

Telepathic pressure. The same weight as the dying god in the cellar — sharper. More coherent.

***...the seed that makes things live. I am what makes things end. We were meant to complete each other.***

A pause.

***...help me. Please. I am so close to being whole again. And I am so tired of being fed through straws.***

---

I don't answer. Not yet. I hold.

"There's an entity behind the pedestal," I tell them. "Telepathic. Asking for help."

I sweep the chamber. Everything the eyes can give me.

The carvings. The root-language symbols. The ley conduits converging. The crown pulsing at the center. A second passage on the south side — larger, proper archway, heavy ward signatures. The main access. The Chancellor's door.

The floor around the pedestal — an inscribed circle, twenty-foot diameter. The entity hasn't moved beyond it.

"It's bound. The circle is containment. It's chained to the crown and the crown is chained to the circle."

I relay everything. Sera and Elara process.

"What kind of help?" Sera says. "Help it finish? Help it eat faster?"

"The containment circle changes things," Elara says. "If it's bound, it didn't build this. Someone else built the cage. Someone else installed the feeding mechanism."

---

I open the channel. Project intent through the ember.

*The crown. Can I take it.*

***...the crown is not mine. The crown is my cage.***

The presence leans forward. Cold light flickering.

***...I did not ask for it. I was dying — truly dying — and a man came with a bargain. He said he could save me. He said the cost would be small.***

The cold light dims. Shame.

***...the cost was not small. I feel them. Every one. Three hundred and forty-seven threads. I taste their essence and it keeps me alive and I hate every swallow.***

***...if you take the crown, the binding breaks. The siphons sever. Every thread, every drain — it stops. Tonight.***

A beat.

***...and I am freed.***

The cold light fixed on me.

***...I will not lie, seed-bearer. I am the Unraveler. What makes things end. Freed, I am what I am. The hunger has changed me. Twelve years of forced feeding — I am more than I was. Less than I was. I am afraid of what I might be.***

The presence contracts. A divine flinch.

***...I might dissipate. Return to the cycle. The natural force of endings, invisible and necessary. Or I might manifest. Become something physical. Powerful. More powerful than I have been in millennia. And confused. And frightened. And very, very hungry.***

***...I am telling you this because you carry the seed. You are the only being in this chamber — perhaps in this world — who could stop me if I become something I don't want to be. The creation energy that completed the cycle beneath the farmhouse could complete me. Or it could unmake me.***

The cold light steadies. Fixed on me. The next words carry the weight of something that has thought about this for twelve years.

***...take the crown. Free me. And if I become a monster — end me. That is the only bargain I will make. And unlike the Chancellor's — mine is honest.***

The ember reads it. No deception. No manipulation. Raw honesty from something ancient and broken.

***...but the crown is almost full. Weeks. When it reaches saturation, the man's bargain completes. He gets immortality. And the three hundred and forty-seven burn. All of them. At once.***

The cold light finds Sera.

***...including her. The one with the empty shelf.***

---

I relay everything. Word for word.

Elara's ink-stained fingers are pressed flat against the chamber wall. Bracing. The scholar in her is screaming — primary source testimony from a bound divine entity. Every theological paper she's ever read just became a footnote. But the woman in her is pale. Because the god feeding on her for eight years just said *I hate every swallow*.

Sera's jaw is iron.

"The man. Ask it who."

*The man who bargained with you. Who.*

***...he came twelve years ago. Already old — not in body. In soul. He had lived beyond his natural span through smaller bargains. He knew the old methods. The encoding. The architecture.***

***...he told me his name as though a god should be impressed by a mortal's title.***

***...Chancellor. He called himself Chancellor.***

---

"Marius Vael," Elara says. Barely audible. "Twelve years."

"He built the cage," Sera says.

I ask the final question. *What did he get from you.*

***...life. Unending life. We are a circuit. The essence flows through the crown into me, through me back into him. He does not age. A hundred and forty years wearing the face of an old man who should have died a century ago.***

***...when the crown is full, the circuit completes permanently. He becomes truly immortal. And the three hundred and forty-seven burn.***

"Weeks," Sera says. "We have weeks."

---

I look at the crown. At the circuit architecture laid open by the ember. Three hundred and forty-seven threads. An anchor point bearing Vael's signature.

"Elara. Can you redirect the crown's anchor? Overwrite Vael's signature with mine?"

She circles the pedestal. Crystal lens. Scribe. Binding ink. Two minutes of furious analysis.

"Three components. The crown collects. Solveth stores. Vael anchors. The anchor is sympathetic — his signature woven into the runes. I can overwrite it. Ten to fifteen minutes inside the circle."

She lays out the implications. Vael loses immortality. A hundred and forty years catches up. I become the anchor. The siphoned essence flows through me. The ember processes it — rivers into an ocean. And from inside the circuit, I can see every thread. Rewrite the system. Dismantle the siphons safely.

"Theoretically," she says.

I look at her.

"Let's do it."

Sera looks at me. Elara looks at me. Two women who've spent years pulling at a thread that leads to the bottom of this building, and the man who walked in eight days ago is the one saying *let's go*.

"For the record," I say, "I'm aware this is insane."

"Noted," Sera says.

"Noted," Elara says.

---

Elara steps across the threshold. The crown accelerates her drain. She gasps. Bears down. The scribe moves with surgical precision — tracing Vael's signature, isolating it, dissolving the redundant threads one by one.

I guard the south passage with Sera. The archway. The chokepoint. Two alcoves flanking the entrance. She takes the right. I take the left. Hand axe. Flint stones. The returning knife with one dose of sleep.

Minutes pass. Elara's voice thins as the drain pulls at her. "First redundant thread removed. Two more."

Solveth watches her work.

***...she is brave, the ink-fingered one. The man who built this was brilliant and cruel. She is brilliant and kind.***

Seven minutes. "Last thread. It's fighting me. The encoding is adaptive — the crown is defending Vael's signature." She bears down. The scribe moving faster. "Got it. Kenji — I need you in the circle. Hand on the crown. The ember fills the space where Vael's signature was."

I step into the circle. The entropy hits like deep water. The cold wraps around me. The ember roars. I put my hand on the crown.

The world detonates.

Not fire. Information. Three hundred and forty-seven threads visible. Every siphon. Every stolen life. A web stretching upward through the Academy, through the city, through the countryside. Individual signatures — a woman who can't light a candle. A man whose healing faded. A retired professor. Sera — the wide pipe, the empty shelf.

And Vael's signature at the center. A hundred and forty years of borrowed life humming in the iron.

Elara's scribe touches the crown. "Beginning the overwrite. Don't let go."

The binding ink burns the old anchor away. The ember fills it. Not because I tell it to — because it *wants* to. Hot gold replacing cold black. My signature inscribing itself into the space where a parasite used to live.

The pain. Not physical. Existential. Three hundred and forty-seven threads of stolen essence hitting an infinite seed. I see their faces. Flash. Flash. Flash. A woman laughing. A man reading. A boy who was going to be a healer and became a clerk who doesn't know why. A girl who could light candles with her mind at six and can't remember why she stopped. Sera throwing a force bolt with both hands. Elara with ink on her fingers and wonder in her eyes.

The INT of nine can't process this. The ember doesn't need it to. Creation doesn't analyze — it *holds*. All of them. Every stolen spark. The infinite seed opens wide and takes the weight.

The ember burns brighter than ever. Gold light pouring from my hand. The runes reorganize around the new anchor.

The circuit completes.

---

Somewhere above — Marius Vael's heart stops. Three seconds. Restarts. A hundred and forty years of borrowed time noticing the rent is no longer paid.

In the chamber, the circuit hums through me. Three hundred and forty-seven threads visible. The architecture open. I reach for Elara's thread.

The ember dissolves it. Eight years of parasitic architecture unmade in two seconds.

Elara makes a sound. A *breath*. The first full breath in eight years. Color floods her face. "Oh. Oh, *gods*."

Sera's thread. Thicker. The wide pipe. Three years of total drain. The ember wraps around it and the thread fights — thicker, deeper roots. The ember burns hotter. Every root. Every tendril. Every anchor point — dissolved. The channels reopened. The shelf rebuilt.

The thread dissolves. Three years. Gone.

At the south passage archway, Sera feels it happen. Her knees buckle. She catches herself on the wall. The sword hits stone — not placed, not sheathed, *dropped*. Sera doesn't drop swords. Her hand comes up. Fingers spread.

Blue-white light.

A force bolt. Fully formed. Stable. Real. The magic stolen three years ago, returned to a framework rebuilt by an infinite seed. Three years of reaching for an empty shelf. Three years of pretending steel was enough. The shelf is full again and the woman who built her life around being both blade and bolt is holding the missing half of herself in her palm.

"You're free, Sera. No more pent up nights in inns trying to do magic."

She looks at me across the chamber. The force bolt in her palm. Tears she will deny until her dying day.

"You absolute—"

She closes her fist. The force bolt intensifies.

"He's coming?" she says.

"Two minutes."

Sword in the right hand. Force bolt in the left. She steps into the center of the archway.

"Let him come."

---

But we don't need to fight. We need to run.

"We have the advantage of time," I tell them. "All we need is to escape with the crown."

The crown off the pedestal. The chamber shudders. Ley threads stretch. The inscribed circle flares and goes dark. Solveth flickers — still bound, the cage is the mechanism, not the location. Where the crown goes, the entity follows.

The crown goes into the Satchel of Holding. Three pounds of blackened iron swallowed by dimensional space. The siphon threads stretch through the fold but hold.

Elara inverts the entropy sensor on the maintenance hatch. Her restored mage-sight and ward expertise making thirty seconds of work look like three years of practice.

Up the shaft. Sera first — the force bolt lighting the way. The blue-white glow steady in her grip, not a flicker, not a waver. She's climbing one-handed because she won't let the bolt go. Me second — Stride-enhanced climbing speed. Elara last — she seals the hatch behind us. Counter-runes drawn with mage-sight she hasn't had in eight years, her hand moving with the precision of someone who forgot she could see in the dark. The entrance exactly as it was.

Through sub-basement two. The nighthollow lab. Ghosts passing workbenches. Elara catches a wobbling flask before it hits the floor — reflex, restored perception, the mage-sight reading the room's layout in real time.

Through sub-basement one. The service corridor. The door. Night air.

Stars.

---

Three people behind an ivy-covered wall. Breathing hard.

"Thanks for your help, ladies. You should have seen your faces once you were no longer all pent up and your magic started working." I adjust the satchel. "Jeez, that gasp of *oh my god* Elara — really that good?"

"Kenji you cannot just WALK AWAY carrying a—"

I'm around the corner.

"—divine artifact containing a CHAINED GOD in a HANDBAG—"

Gone.

Behind me — two women on cold ground. One with a sword and a restored force bolt. One with a scribe and eight years of returned mage-sight. Both staring at the empty space.

"He put a god in his satchel," Elara says. "He put an entropy god in a satchel and walked to an inn."

Sera sheathes her sword. Slowly.

"He does this."

"You warned me."

"The warning was insufficient."

"I'm going to kill him."

"Not before I do."

"We could collaborate."

"I'll draft a plan. Tomorrow."

---

The Silver Draft. Back door. My room. The lock clicks.

The Satchel of Holding on my lap. Inside — the Hollow Crown. Three hundred and forty-five threads humming through the ember.

***...seed-bearer. The empty chamber. The man is there. I can feel him. He is afraid. For the first time in a hundred and forty years.***

A pause.

***...thank you. For not destroying the crown. For not destroying me. For choosing the leash instead of the sword.***

***...I will try to be worth the mercy.***

The pressure fades. The entity settling into the dimensional space. A prisoner transferred to a kinder cell.

I eat. Rations from the satchel. Perfectly preserved. I lie back on the bed. The satchel on my chest. The crown inside. The ember burning steady — hotter, deeper, processing three hundred and forty-five stolen lives through an infinite seed and holding.

Tomorrow. Aldwin at dawn. Edwyn's presentation. A Chancellor aging in real time, hunting for his crown.

And me. Walking into all of it with a chained god in my satchel and two furious women planning my murder.

Day eight. The longest day since the mud.

My eyes close. The ember holds the circuit. The heartbeat syncs with my breathing.

I sleep.

---

DING — LEVEL 6 — PERK SELECTION AVAILABLE

The ember didn't just deepen this time. It *restructured*. The circuit — three hundred and forty-five threads of entropy-stolen essence flowing through a seed of infinite creation — has changed the architecture of what I am. The power is denser. More articulate. The connection between will and magic not just tighter but *wider*. More channels. More options. The ember learned something tonight about what it means to hold entropy in one hand and creation in the other.

KENJI
Human — Blade Channeler — Sorcerer Swordsman
Level 6 — Outlander

Weeks. Maybe less.

The clock is running.

End of Chapter Twelve.
# KENJI

## *Day Nine — The Dramatic Little Bastard*

---

Dawn. The Silver Draft. The bed. The ceiling. The satchel on my chest.

Thump. Thump. Thump.

Not my heartbeat. Alongside it. The Hollow Crown pulsing inside the dimensional fold. Three hundred and forty-five threads humming through the ember like a choir in a language I'm still learning. The circuit is constant now — a background awareness that wasn't there two days ago. The ley web beneath the city the way I feel my own pulse. The Academy tower a bright knot. The graduates — scattered across the region — faint individual notes in a vast chord.

The ember is different this morning. Not just deeper. Wider. Level six. The long rest processed the circuit the way sleep processes a hard lesson. The creation energy didn't just absorb it. It organized it.

New spell slots. Level three. Two of them. Empty chambers waiting. And the perk — the second perk — something crystallizing at the edge of perception. The ember has changed. The man who touches gods has been changed by the touching.

I eat. Bread, smoked meat, an apple from the satchel. Perfectly preserved. The furnace accepts it sitting in pre-dawn dark with a god in my bag.

---

Full gear. Ironwood armor. Chest piece. Shoulder guards. Longsword left hip. Hand axe right. Returning knife on belt. Windrunner Boots. Satchel of Holding cross-body — the Crown inside, invisible, the heartbeat muffled.

The circuit tells me things without being asked. The ley web is agitated. The Academy tower pulsing irregularly — the arrhythmia of a system that lost its core component. The threads are flowing into me now, through the satchel, and the web hasn't fully recalibrated.

---

The common room. Garrett at the corner table. Coffee. Ledger.

"You look different."

"New day."

"No. Different. Heavier. Not weight. *Presence*. Like there's more of you."

"Leveled up overnight. New spells. Deeper reserves."

"Hm." He accepts it. "The guild contract lead panned out — merchant consortium running northern caravans. They need escorts. I'm meeting their factor at noon."

He slides a paper across. "Brindle's courier arrived. The Council highway contract reached the Antler. She signed. The guild is officially operational. First monthly payment in three weeks."

He sets two glass vials on the table. Dark green liquid. The sharp chemical smell of something that doesn't want to be touched.

Bittershade. From Edwyn. Ready before dawn, as promised.

"Edwyn said to tell you: *remember they feel everything*."

---

The Academy gates. Dawn. The guards wave me through — but one looks a beat longer than yesterday. Something in the Academy has changed overnight and even the guards feel it.

The courtyard. Fewer students than yesterday. Clusters of conversation.

"—felt it last night, around midnight—"

"—the tower lights flickered—"

"—the Chancellor cancelled his morning appointments—"

The Chancellor cancelled his morning appointments. The cover story — ley fluctuation — is holding. But Vael isn't in his office. He's somewhere doing something about the empty chamber beneath his feet.

---

The eastern training grounds. Aldwin on the bench. Same stillness. But the staff isn't leaned against the bench — it's in his hands. Across his knees. The grip isn't casual. The knuckles white.

"Sit down."

I sit.

"Something happened in this Academy last night. Around midnight. The ley web convulsed. Every ward flickered. My staff—" He lifts it. "—woke me up. It's been tuned to the network for forty years. Never done that before."

He sets it down.

"This morning the Chancellor cancelled all appointments. His office is locked. The sub-basement guards reported nothing unusual but the wards reported a micro-anomaly on the level-three sensor at twelve-oh-three AM. Three minutes after midnight shift change."

The grey eyes.

"You came here two days ago. Yesterday you cleared my gauntlet. Last night the ley web convulsed for the first time in three centuries." He taps the staff. "I don't believe in coincidences."

"What did you do, Kenji?"

---

"What are you talking about, old man? I was busy helping two pent-up beautiful women last night. I even made one gasp oh my god." I wave my hands in his face. "Cast one of your *you're a wizard, Aldwin* spells and read my mind if you can."

He stares at me.

"You're a wizard, Aldwin," he repeats. Flat.

He reaches forward. Two fingers — scarred, knotted — press against my forehead.

He looks inside.

---

I lay out the memories like a card dealer choosing which cards face up. The Perfect Recall curating the presentation. The ember keeping the background dark, the context stripped.

What Aldwin sees:

A warded room. Elara. Her wrist in my hand. Eyes going wide. The gasp — "*Oh. Oh, gods.*" Color flooding her face.

No seal visible. No threads. No entropy. Just a man touching a woman's wrist and her reaction.

A fountain. Sera. Her forearm in my hand. Knees buckling. The gasp. Tears. "*It was there. For a second.*"

No force bolt visible. No siphon. Just a man touching a woman's arm and her coming undone.

My voice: "*You should have seen your faces once you were no longer all pent up.*" Elara: "*KENJI you cannot just WALK AWAY—*" Sera: "*He does this.*"

---

Aldwin's fingers leave my forehead.

"You're telling me that last night — while the ley web was experiencing its first major convulsion — you were making Instructor Ash gasp. And making Sera buckle." He looks at me. "By touching their... forearms."

A pause.

"I'm seventy years old. I've been half-deaf for twenty. But I am not stupid."

He sits back down.

"What you showed me doesn't explain the ley web. But the fact that you curated it — shaped it, used that perfect memory to present exactly what you wanted — tells me something more important."

He leans forward.

"You're hiding something. Something involving Elara. Something involving Sera. Something that shook the foundations of this Academy." The grey eyes. "And you're hiding it behind the most elaborate *I was busy with women* excuse I've heard in four decades."

He plants the staff.

"Is this Academy in danger?"

"Depends on me, Aldwin. I'll make a deal — you show me something cool, and I'll whip something out of my bag that answers your question. I'd like to learn a summoned frost sword."

"You're *negotiating* with me. I ask if the Academy is in danger and you're negotiating."

He doesn't throw me off the training ground.

"Show me something cool," he repeats.

---

He teaches. Not theory. Not formulae. The way a man with forty years and no time teaches.

"Frost is not ice. Frost is *stillness*. Cold is the absence of motion. Your ember makes things exist — make stillness exist. Give it form. Give it an edge."

He demonstrates. The ice sword in his hand — clouded white, blue edge, smoking in the morning air. Then dismisses it.

"Don't copy me. Ask the ember what stillness looks like when it's sharp."

The ember considers. The creation energy takes the lattice, the framework, the idea of motion being removed. And the circuit adds something. The 345 threads carrying stolen essence — some belongs to mages who understood cold. Their knowledge is in the current. Their vocabulary is in the ember now.

And Solveth. What is cold but the ending of warmth? What is frost but entropy applied to motion?

The ember and the circuit and the whisper of a chained god converge.

The sword forms in my hand.

Not Aldwin's ice sword. Darker. Blue-black, the color of deep winter midnight. Dense, not transparent. The edge smokes with cold that has a faintly green tinge — the entropy echo. The crossguard is jagged crystal. Sharp enough to cut.

The cold radiates. Not just temperature — *intent*. The air thickens. Moisture freezes. The packed earth frosts in a two-foot radius. Everything near this weapon is being told to slow down.

I'm holding entropy. Not fighting it. Not completing it the way I did in the cellar. *Wielding* it. The ember made this blade and the blade carries endings and I can feel the difference in my bones — creation that chooses to end things is not destruction. It's winter. Necessary. Temporary. The sleep before the growth.

"That's not what I taught you," Aldwin says.

"The ember had opinions."

"Your ember always has opinions." He reads the blade. "There's something in the frost that shouldn't be there. That green tinge. The Crown. The circuit. It's influencing your conjurations."

"Is that a problem?"

Five seconds.

"Not yet. But watch it. Creation and entropy in the same blade is either the most balanced weapon I've ever seen or the most dangerous."

---

I dismiss the Frost Fang. The blade dissolves into cold vapor. The frost radius fades.

"Your turn," I say. "A deal's a deal."

I reach into the satchel. My fingers find the blackened iron. The crawling runes warm against my skin. I pull the Hollow Crown out.

The training ground changes.

The ley web beneath the packed earth flares. The ward runes from yesterday's gauntlet glow. The stone owl fountain gurgles louder. Every enchantment within a hundred feet wakes up.

Aldwin's staff screams. Bright blue. The ley-tuned instrument responding to the object that was the convergence point for three hundred years of infrastructure.

He looks at the Crown. The grey eyes — forty years in this Academy, forty years walking above something he never knew existed.

"Gods. That's a convergence anchor. That's what the ley web was built around."

"Sub-basement three. Below everything. In a chamber older than this institution."

"Who."

"That's the part I'm not telling you yet. Not because I don't trust you — because the person who put this down there has been here longer than you have."

He stares. The grey eyes recalculating everything. Forty years. The seals. The graduates. The fading. The deaths. The staff in his hands has stopped tapping — the first time I've seen it completely still. Aldwin's constant rhythm, his thinking heartbeat, silenced by the weight of what he's looking at.

"A convergence anchor. Collecting what."

"Essence. Magical essence. Siphoned from graduates through their Assignment Seals."

The staff creaks in his grip.

"The seals. Every student I've certified. Every combat mage I've trained. They walked out with a drain woven into—"

He stops. Looks at his hands. The scarred hands that shook the hands of eleven combat mages. Seven dead. Did the drain weaken them? Did it contribute to—

The thought crosses his face. The horror as revision. Every death. Every decline. Every former student who just seemed to fade.

"How long."

"Twelve years. Three hundred and forty-seven graduates."

"And the person who built it."

"Is in this Academy right now. And they know the Crown is gone."

Aldwin sits down. Not on the bench. On the ground. The staff across his knees. The most dangerous man in the building sitting in the dirt processing the fact that his life's work has been a farm.

Ten seconds.

"Last night. Sera and Elara. That's what the gasping was. You removed their siphons."

"I touched their seals with the ember. The creation energy dissolved the entropy threads."

"They gasped." He looks at me. The ghost of something that might have been a smile in a universe where he hadn't just learned his institution is a slaughterhouse. "The oh-my-god gasp. You dramatic little bastard."

I pull him to his feet.

"I don't know who built it," he says. "You won't tell me. Fine. But are they stronger than me?"

"Potentially. Twelve years of accumulated stolen essence."

"Then you need to be stronger than both of us." He plants the staff. "Put that thing away. Tomorrow. Dawn. I teach you something that requires you to trust me completely. And you tell me who put that Crown in the basement."

He walks toward the colonnade.

"Dramatic little bastard," he mutters. But the staff taps with a rhythm that sounds like approval.

Dramatic little bastard. I'll take it. Add it to the list — Blade Channeler, Combat Mage Number Twelve, Crown Bearer, Dramatic Little Bastard. The resume is getting interesting.

I put the Crown back in the satchel. The ley web settles. I recast the Frost Fang — the blue-black blade reforming in my hand. Twelve hours. The green tinge curling from the edge like breath in winter air.

---

END OF CHAPTER THIRTEEN — NO LEVEL UP (No Long Rest)

The morning sun on the training ground. Frost melting where the new blade touched the earth. A green tinge fading from the air. The most dangerous man in the Academy walking away with knowledge that changes everything he believed about his life's work.

And in my satchel — the god and the Crown and 345 threads humming steady. The ember holding it all. Creation and entropy and stillness and the particular warmth of trust given in exchange for a dramatic little truth.

Aldwin will figure out who built the Crown. By tomorrow he won't need me to tell him. The old man's grey eyes have been reading this Academy for forty years. Now they know what they're looking for.

The afternoon holds Edwyn's presentation. The evening holds whatever Vael is planning. The night holds the unknown.

But this morning — this morning I learned that frost is the ending of warmth. And the ember learned that endings can be a weapon too.


# KENJI

## *Day Nine (continued) — Two Combat Mages*

---

Sera arrives in four minutes. Through the colonnade at a pace that's technically walking and functionally advancing. Dark leathers. Sword on hip. The face of a woman who received a three-word summons from the most dangerous man in the Academy and came armed.

She sees me. Then Aldwin. Then the frost residue on the training ground. Then the Frost Fang in my hand — the blue-black blade with the green entropy edge that didn't exist yesterday.

"New sword."

"Learned it this morning."

"Of course you did."

She looks at Aldwin. Respect. Deference. The relationship between a certified combat mage and the man who certified her.

"Master Aldwin. You summoned me."

"He summoned you." Aldwin nods at me. "I'm just the messenger service."

Sera looks at me. The professional mask on — but underneath, the awareness of everything. The Crown. The crawl. The force bolt in her palm. The tears she'll deny. And the particular fury of a woman who was simultaneously saved and insulted.

"What do you need, Kenji."

---

"I need you to teach me how to fight with two weapons. Not the cage — something that lets me attack twice in the same action. The longsword and the Frost Fang together."

She draws her arming sword. Holds it right. Extends her left — a force bolt forming, elongating, solidifying into a short blade of compressed energy.

My eyebrows rise. She didn't have that yesterday.

"My magic came back with interest." Flat. Not explaining.

She settles into a stance I haven't seen — wider than the cage, lower, both weapons forward. Fluid.

"The cage is defense. A wall. This is different." She moves — the arming sword cuts lateral, the force blade follows from the opposite angle. A scissors pattern. "Two weapons. Two lines of attack. Same motion. The first opens the guard. The second punishes it."

She resets.

"Twin Fang. I learned it third year. Original technique used matching short swords." She looks at my weapons. "You're not matching. Longsword heavy, long, physical. Frost Fang lighter, shorter, magical. You can't mirror. You complement."

She looks at Aldwin. "May I use the grounds?"

"It's your certification. Teach."

---

"Draw both. Longsword right, Frost Fang left."

The longsword — merchant steel, familiar. The Frost Fang — blue-black, smoking, green entropy curling into the air. Two weapons. Steel and stillness.

"The longsword leads. Heavier, longer, more damage. The Frost Fang follows — shorter, faster, the finishing strike. Think of it as punctuation. The longsword writes the sentence. The Frost Fang adds the period."

She demonstrates slow — leading cut, body rotation, trailing weapon following the torque.

"The rotation generates momentum in your off-hand. Use it. The Frost Fang comes around on the back of the longsword's arc. Not separate. Continuation."

The dummy first. The headless one that survived the gauntlet.

The longsword cuts right to left. Body rotates. The Frost Fang follows left to right, trailing the torque. Both blades connect within a half second. The longsword bites canvas. The Frost Fang freezes where it touches.

"Rough. Timing's off. The Frost Fang arrived late. Again. Faster. Don't think about the off-hand — let the rotation carry it."

Better. The longsword leads and the Frost Fang rides its wake. Both cuts in a window too tight for a human opponent to block the second.

"Now the problem." She draws. "Against me. Half speed."

The diagonal. I block with the longsword — instinct, the cage. The Frost Fang hangs. Dead weight. The dual-wield offense vanishes the moment I go defensive.

"That. When you defend, the off-hand dies. The cage used one blade for everything. Twin Fang needs you to separate them. During defense, the Frost Fang doesn't strike — it positions. Somewhere the enemy doesn't want it to be."

The diagonal again. The longsword catches it. But this time my left hand moves — the Frost Fang drops low, pointing at her knee. Not striking. Threatening. Frost smoking six inches from her leg.

She sees it. Has to adjust. The follow-up costs her a quarter-second.
